I just completed the 6 week challenge with DC fitness. It was a total success - so I wanted to share my story to not only show appreciation for the program, but to also advise others others look to achieve their fitness goals.

Moving to LA a year and a half ago was difficult. It was a move I had to make, but the challenges that come with a cross country move took a toll on my mind and body.

2 months ago, I came across one of those Instagram ads about getting fit in 6 weeks. I was skeptical, but I needed to get fit. As a constant athlete growing up, I was not happy with where my body was at and needed a change. So I put the money down and was all in.

The program offers 3 main facets: Fitness, Nutrition, and Accountability.  Working out 3 times a week with the DC team ended up becoming some I looked forward to, rather that something I dreaded. I was able to build great relationships with each trainer, who truly cared able my progress and success. I was surprised by how supportive all the other gym members were as well - but I guess that what happens when there is a mutual goal.

Stay true to the regiment this program lays out for you, and you will see results in 6 weeks. I recommend the challenge to anybody looking to improve their physical and mental health, through a challenge that provides all the necessary tools to succeed.

< review>
what a journey it was when I first started coming here! I learned about this place from a Snapchat ad I saw.  Basically, it was promoting a six week challenge for a gym located in Brentwood.  I was called and told that the goal is to lose either 25 lbs or 6% BF within 6 weeks.  The catch is that you must pay a fee, but it will be reimbursed if you meet either goal.  It may seem tough, but if you stick through their workouts and meal plans, then you should come out ahead.

None of this is easy, don't get me mistaken.  It will be tough at first getting used to a drastically different meal plan, as well as being worked out rigorously, more than you're probably used to.  As time goes on, it'll get easier, but you should still push yourself in workouts and don't fall into temptations in your diet.

Workouts were tough, but they were also great.  While they were hard, you generally feel good afterwards, as if you have a boost in energy, despite being sore.  I feel this also helped me on my hike to Half Dome, which happened around the Week 4 mark for me.  It made it easier.  Big shoutouts to Sequoia, TJ, Cornelius, Ezekiel, Brent, Dylan, and Ambra for all helping me in their own ways.  They are all awesome people (:

Finally, I finished with this challenge at 6.8% BF loss and I believe roughly 21 lbs lost (From 22.1% -> 15.3% and 172.1 lbs -> 151.?). < Text>
This place is great for both south Indian breakfast items as well as traditional meals for lunch/dinner options. We went to this place back to back twice in two days as we liked the place. We ordered idly, schezwan noodles, cut mirchi bajji and pongal vada the first time, everything was good, no disappointment at all. The service is comparatively fast, you get your items within 10min or less after ordering. The menu is reasonably priced.
The schezwann noodles are very spicy (I usually eat very spicy food and this was just a little bit too much for me but I could eat it) and the people there warn you when you order it, take their word, its very spicy. We got mini tiffin plate and schezwann fried rice the next time we went and the tiffin plate is a good combination of all the tiffin items available there and it is very filling. The schezwann fried rice was even more spicier than the noodles. Be careful when you order this item. Everything else seems to be very good.<//Text>

< Text>
This restaurant has large space. Reminds me of udipi hotel back in India.
My favorites are mini-tiffin & Bhimas thali.
They have good dosas too.
They took lot of time to get my order. I have ordered Bhimas thali.
I really found their 'podis'(powders) in the menu to be interesting. The waiter/ owner mentioned that those powders cannot be provided as sides, though I'm willing to pay. I'm fine with that.
Then another customer next to me, asked him in Tamil, for one of the powders (podi). Waiter finally gave him and me one podi (powder) along the ghee. It was good..!
Thali was good.
Thali consists of the following items.
1. Rice
2. curries(made with some beans/ vegetable)
3. sambar
4. rasam
5. curd
6. dessert.

Then in-between when I needed extra rice, I had to wait for almost 15 min to talk to a waiter.
How can you serve customers properly during busy hours, If you are unable to handle, when the restaurant is only 25% full (approx)?

The food is actually good (felt close to home food & can be improved)  but the management is ruining with their bad service.
Please Hire more waiters to handle the restaurant properly..!<//Text>

< review>
The waiters are quite friendly but some of them don't seem to understand English well which lead to difficult communication. The menu doesn't have description what the dishes are and may be confusing to non-Indian-food-savvy folks but I appreciate them taking the time to explain. From the description online I thought they have "vegetarian options" (meaning there are meat options or substitutes too) but apparently not, they're all veggies. Overall, I appreciate that the place is very clean, no heavy food smell, and service is quick, but it feels like the business is set up to cater mostly to Indian crowds (limited hours, no description on menu, and employees don't all have command of the English language).</review>

< Review>
They have some nice food options for Indo-Chinese, South Indian, and North Indian food-lovers....  I have tried their gobi munchurian, veg fried rice, hakka noodles, idli manchurian, sweet corn soup; they were all delicious and reminded me of Indo-Chinese food native to Mumbai.  As for South Indian food, which seems to be their specialty, my favorites have been their idli plate, idli vadai plate, coriander dosa, onion rawa dosa, custom uttapams (onion, tomato, peas), filter coffee (on the bitter side with good amount of chicory), and masala chai.  Their paav bhaji had never failed to impress, so when in the mood for North Indian food, that's what I always order.  Their desserts are good too: of course their rawa kesari is yummy, as are their ice creams (tutti fruity being my favorite).  Their kitchen is a bit exposed, but otherwise there is usually enough seating, prices are quite reasonable, there's always parking, and the staff is pleasant and hospitable.<//Review>

< userid>
107841640861519475435< /userid>
<username>Sivaramakrishnan Vaidyanathan<//username><date>1515119243474< /date><rate>4</rate>< Review>
Subsidized Indian vegetarian restaurant in Milpitas on Able St close to Great Mall. It뗩 all South Indian  vegetarian and offers no meat options.

There is a North Indian and South Indian Thaali here. Additionally, they also offer a spicy South Indian Thaali but I wouldn뗪 recommend it if you aren뗪 used to spice levels from Andhra Pradesh and Tamil Nadu. Thaali rate is $9.50 and I think it is value for its price compared to other restaurants in Bay Area. They offer South Indian snack options, indo-Chinese, appetizers like Soups and beverages. They are all reasonably priced. Do try their Chili Bhaji if you like that popular South Indian snack or the spicy Schezwan fried rice which is a popular Indian flavorful imitation of East Asian fried rice.

Parking shouldn뗪 be a problem here anytime of the day. They are generally open for lunch after 10.30 AM and close briefly during the afternoon before opening again for dinner at 6PM.< /Review>

<Text>After a shopping stint at the Great Mall in Milpitas, our family and that of a friend of ours wanted to get an Indian dinner. My friend suggested Tirupathi Bhimas- a place I have never been to but one that my wife had visited and had a decent opinion about. I agreed to give the place a shot- if not anything, atleast to get a review in (such if the power of writing my own blog :) )

We arrived pretty late on a Saturday night. The place was reasonably crowded but not really full. The waiter having deciphered that we all shared a common language, decided to pitch in with recommendations so forceful it was almost as if he knew wanted us to eat. It was almost comical seeing him push what he thought we should be eating.

We had two tired and hungry kids. So we decided to order a simple curd rice for one of them while the other was going to share his mother뗩 South Indian thali. For the rest of the group, we ordered an adai avial (adai resembles a dosa but is much thicker because of the lentil batter it uses), szechuan fried rice and another plate of curd rice. The curd rice arrived quickly and we realised almost immediately that it was spicy. Yes, you are allowed to ask- how and why in the world is curd rice spicy. Beats me. The pattern was starting to show. My wife who ordered the thali complained that everything was a tad on the spicy side. She had to use the kesari in her thali to give my son his meal from hers. My szechuan fried rice was spicy beyond expectations. To be fair, I was warned that it was a spicy dish. Just that I did not anticipate the level of spice it carried. The kitchen was closing soon. I had to order a cup of the rava kesari just to quench the spice in my mouth. All in all, the spice was a tad too much for all of us to handle.</Text><user_id>113224422168461556238<//user_id>< name>
Rangaprabhu Parthasarathy<//name>
